  <COMMENT line1="500" col1="1" line2="500" col2="80" start="82501" end="82580">################################################################################</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="502" col1="1" line2="502" col2="44" start="82831" end="82874">#' Plot a relative log expression (RLE) plot</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="503" col1="1" line2="503" col2="2" start="82996" end="82997">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="504" col1="1" line2="504" col2="82" start="83161" end="83242">#' Produce a relative log expression (RLE) plot of one or more transformations of </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="505" col1="1" line2="505" col2="26" start="83326" end="83351">#' cell expression values.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="506" col1="1" line2="506" col2="2" start="83491" end="83492">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="507" col1="1" line2="507" col2="54" start="83656" end="83709">#' @param object an \code{SingleCellExperiment} object</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="508" col1="1" line2="508" col2="80" start="83821" end="83900">#' @param exprs_mats named list of expression matrices. Entries can either be a </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="509" col1="1" line2="509" col2="79" start="83986" end="84064">#' character string, in which case the corresponding expression matrix will be </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="510" col1="1" line2="510" col2="91" start="84151" end="84241">#' extracted from the SingleCellExperiment \code{object}, or a matrix of expression values.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="511" col1="1" line2="511" col2="84" start="84316" end="84399">#' @param exprs_logged logical vector of same length as \code{exprs_mats} indicating</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="512" col1="1" line2="512" col2="82" start="84481" end="84562">#' whether the corresponding entry in \code{exprs_mats} contains logged expression</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="513" col1="1" line2="513" col2="46" start="84646" end="84691">#' values (\code{TRUE}) or not (\code{FALSE}).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="514" col1="1" line2="514" col2="85" start="84811" end="84895">#' @param colour_by character string defining the column of \code{colData(object)} to</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="515" col1="1" line2="515" col2="81" start="84976" end="85056">#' be used as a factor by which to colour the points in the plot. Alternatively, </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="516" col1="1" line2="516" col2="83" start="85141" end="85223">#' a data frame with one column, containing values to map to colours for all cells.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="517" col1="1" line2="517" col2="81" start="85306" end="85386">#' @param style character(1), either \code{"minimal"} (default) or \code{"full"},</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="518" col1="1" line2="518" col2="84" start="85471" end="85554">#' defining the boxplot style to use. \code{"minimal"} uses Tufte-style boxplots and</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="519" col1="1" line2="519" col2="68" start="85636" end="85703">#' is fast for large numbers of cells. \code{"full"} uses the usual </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="520" col1="1" line2="520" col2="80" start="85801" end="85880">#' \code{\link{ggplot2}} and is more detailed and flexible, but can take a long </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="521" col1="1" line2="521" col2="35" start="85966" end="86000">#' time to plot for large datasets.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="522" col1="1" line2="522" col2="77" start="86131" end="86207">#' @param legend character, specifying how the legend(s) be shown? Default is</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="523" col1="1" line2="523" col2="80" start="86296" end="86375">#' \code{"auto"}, which hides legends that have only one level and shows others.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="524" col1="1" line2="524" col2="44" start="86461" end="86504">#' Alternative is "none" (hide all legends).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="525" col1="1" line2="525" col2="76" start="86626" end="86701">#' @param order_by_colour logical, should cells be ordered (grouped) by the </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="526" col1="1" line2="526" col2="77" start="86791" end="86867">#' \code{colour_by} variable? Default is \code{TRUE}. Useful for visualising </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="527" col1="1" line2="527" col2="58" start="86956" end="87013">#' differences between batches or experimental conditions.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="528" col1="1" line2="528" col2="73" start="87121" end="87193">#' @param ncol integer, number of columns for the facetting of the plot. </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="529" col1="1" line2="529" col2="16" start="87286" end="87301">#' Default is 1.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="530" col1="1" line2="530" col2="78" start="87451" end="87528">#' @param ... further arguments passed to \code{\link[ggplot2]{geom_boxplot}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="531" col1="1" line2="531" col2="2" start="87616" end="87617">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="532" col1="1" line2="532" col2="31" start="87781" end="87811">#' @return a ggplot plot object</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="533" col1="1" line2="533" col2="2" start="87946" end="87947">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="534" col1="1" line2="534" col2="12" start="88111" end="88122">#' @details </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="535" col1="1" line2="535" col2="86" start="88276" end="88361">#' Unwanted variation can be highly problematic and so its detection is often crucial.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="536" col1="1" line2="536" col2="80" start="88441" end="88520">#' Relative log expression (RLE) plots are a powerful tool for visualising such </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="537" col1="1" line2="537" col2="76" start="88606" end="88681">#' variation in high dimensional data. RLE plots are particularly useful for</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="538" col1="1" line2="538" col2="78" start="88771" end="88848">#' assessing whether a procedure aimed at removing unwanted variation, i.e. a </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="539" col1="1" line2="539" col2="79" start="88936" end="89014">#' normalisation procedure, has been successful. These plots, while originally </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="540" col1="1" line2="540" col2="81" start="89101" end="89181">#' devised for gene expression data from microarrays, can also be used to reveal </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="541" col1="1" line2="541" col2="82" start="89266" end="89347">#' unwanted variation in single-cell expression data, where such variation can be </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="542" col1="1" line2="542" col2="15" start="89431" end="89445">#' problematic.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="543" col1="1" line2="543" col2="3" start="89596" end="89598">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="544" col1="1" line2="544" col2="80" start="89761" end="89840">#' If style is "full", as usual with boxplots, the box shows the inter-quartile </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="545" col1="1" line2="545" col2="80" start="89926" end="90005">#' range and whiskers extend no more than 1.5 * IQR from the hinge (the 25th or </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="546" col1="1" line2="546" col2="82" start="90091" end="90172">#' 75th percentile). Data beyond the whiskers are called outliers and are plotted </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="547" col1="1" line2="547" col2="72" start="90256" end="90327">#' individually. The median (50th percentile) is shown with a white bar.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="548" col1="1" line2="548" col2="3" start="90421" end="90423">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="549" col1="1" line2="549" col2="79" start="90586" end="90664">#' If style is "minimal", then median is shown with a circle, the IQR in a grey</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="550" col1="1" line2="550" col2="81" start="90751" end="90831">#' line, and "whiskers" (as defined above) for the plots are shown with coloured </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="551" col1="1" line2="551" col2="52" start="90916" end="90967">#' lines. No outliers are shown for this plot style.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="552" col1="1" line2="552" col2="2" start="91081" end="91082">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="553" col1="1" line2="553" col2="15" start="91246" end="91260">#' @references </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="554" col1="1" line2="554" col2="94" start="91411" end="91504">#' Gandolfo LC, Speed TP. RLE Plots: Visualising Unwanted Variation in High Dimensional Data. </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="555" col1="1" line2="555" col2="68" start="91576" end="91643">#' arXiv [stat.ME]. 2017. Available: http://arxiv.org/abs/1704.03590</COMMENT>
